Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Thought:
  Obstructive sleep apnea is a condition where breathing is repeatedly interrupted during sleep.
  The obstruction may be due to various reasons, including physical blockage of the airway.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma and dentigerous cyst are odontogenic cysts that are unlikely to cause obstructive sleep apnea.
  Orbital fracture is a type of facial injury that affects the eye socket and is not related to the airway.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis refers to the fixation of the temporomandibular joint, which may limit jaw movement and potentially cause airway obstruction.
  Therefore, the most likely cause of obstructive sleep apnea from the given options is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Obstructive sleep apnoea is caused by a blockage of the airway during sleep.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma and Dentigerous cyst are both benign odontogenic tumors which may cause swelling of the jaw, but they are unlikely to cause airway obstruction during sleep.
  Orbital fracture is a fracture of the bony socket that holds the eye and not related to obstructive sleep apnoea.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition where the jaw is unable to open due to fusion of the jaw bone to the skull bone. This can cause airway obstruction and lead to obstructive sleep apnoea.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.
Action: Answer("D")

Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient is 60 years old and had a myocardial infarction 2 weeks back.
  The lipid profile reveals low HDL, high LDL, and high TG levels.
  The preferred treatment for this patient should be a combination of medications to lower cholesterol and triglyceride levels.
  Rosuvastatin is a statin that lowers LDL and can mildly increase HDL cholesterol.
  Fenofibrate is a fibric acid derivative that lowers triglyceride levels and can mildly increase HDL cholesterol.
  Atorvastatin is another statin that lowers LDL cholesterol.
  Based on the lipid profile of the patient, a combination of Rosuvastatin and Fenofibrate would be preferred.
  Answer: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The patient had a myocardial infarction 2 weeks back.
  The lipid profile shows high TG levels (276 mg/dL).
  High TG levels are treated with fibrates.
  The LDL levels are mildly elevated (126 mg/dL).
  The preferred statin for secondary prevention in patients with previous myocardial infarction is atorvastatin.
  Rosuvastatin is a good alternative to atorvastatin.
  A combination of statin and fibrate may increase the risk of myopathy.
  Therefore, the preferred treatment for this patient is Atorvastatin 80 mg.
Action: Answer("D")

Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Thought:
The floor of the third ventricle is a part of the ventricular system present in the brain.
It is located between the left and right thalami.
The optic stalk, third nerve, infundibulum, and mammillary body are all structures present on the floor of the third ventricle.
Therefore, none of the choices are correct and the answer is "None of the above."

Action: Answer("None of the above")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The floor of the third ventricle is formed by the hypothalamus.
  The optic stalk and mammillary body are present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  The infundibulum is a funnel-shaped structure that connects the hypothalamus to the pituitary gland.
  The third nerve is not present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Third nerve.
Action: Answer("B")

  The infundibulum is a stalk-like structure that connects the pituitary gland to the brain.
  The mammillary body is a small, rounded protrusion on the underside of the brain.
  The optic stalk, third nerve, and infundibulum are present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Mammillary body.

Choices:

  B: Sickle cell anemia patient

Cystic fibrosis patients are at high risk of developing pneumonia, so they need to be vaccinated against it.
Sickle cell anemia patients are also at high risk of developing pneumonia due to their weakened immune system.
Recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis patients are not at high risk for pneumonia.
Children less than 2 years old are usually vaccinated with PCV-13 instead of PPV-23.

  Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis may have bacterial infections that can be caused by pneumococcal bacteria.
  Children less than 2 years old are at increased risk of pneumococcal infections.
  Therefore, PPV-23 is most beneficial for all of the given choices.
Action: Answer("E") - None of the Above.
Response 9:
Thought:

It is used to protect against pneumococcal disease.
The risk of pneumococcal disease is high among the elderly, immunocompromised individuals, and those with certain medical conditions.
Cystic fibrosis and sickle cell anemia are medical conditions that increase the risk of pneumococcal disease.
Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis may benefit from other vaccines that protect against the common causes of these conditions.
Children less than 2 years may benefit from another vaccine called PCV-13.

  A: Primary hypothyrodism
  B: Pituitary tumor
  C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma
  D: TSH resistance

  Therefore, the most likely diagnosis is C: TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma.

Nutrient agar is a general-purpose medium that supports the growth of many different types of bacteria, so it is not selective for Streptococcus rnutans.
Mitis Salivarius Bacitracin Agar is a selective and differential medium used for the isolation of Streptococcus mutans from oral samples.
Tellurite medium is used for the isolation and identification of Corynebacterium diphtheriae, not for Streptococcus rnutans.

Topic: Dental
Question: Pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in
primary teeth because of:
Choices:
  A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young
  B: Increased blood supply through the wide apex
  C: Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth
  D: Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young
Response 0:
Thought:
  Pulpectomy and pulp capping are procedures done to treat damaged dental pulp.
  Primary teeth are baby teeth that eventually fall out and are replaced by permanent teeth.
  The question is asking why pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in primary teeth.
  Increased odontoblastic activity means that there is more activity in the cells that form dentin, which is the hard part of the tooth.
  Increased blood supply through the wide apex means that there is more blood flow to the tooth, which can help with healing.
  Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth means that there is more of the soft tissue inside the tooth that can be treated.
  Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young teeth means that there is less of the connective tissue that can interfere with treatment.
  Based on this, increased odontoblastic activity and increased blood supply through the wide apex seem like the most plausible reasons for why pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in primary teeth.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Pulpectomy and pulp capping are dental procedures performed to treat the pulp of the tooth.
  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth that develop in a child's mouth.
  These teeth are replaced by permanent teeth as the child grows.
  Primary teeth have a larger pulp chamber than permanent teeth.
  Primary teeth have a wider apical foramen than permanent teeth.
  Odontoblastic activity is higher in primary teeth than in permanent teeth.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young.
Action: Answer("A")

Topic: Dental
Question: Reactive oxygen metabolite in lysosomes is released by
Choices:
  A: Peroxidase
  B: NADPH oxidase
  C: Superoxide dismutase
  D: Catalase
Response 0:
Thought:
  Reactive oxygen metabolites are harmful to cells.
  Lysosomes are organelles within cells that contain enzymes to break down waste materials.
  Release of reactive oxygen metabolites from lysosomes can cause damage to the cell.
  Peroxidase, NADPH oxidase, and catalase are enzymes that can help break down reactive oxygen metabolites.
  Superoxide dismutase is an enzyme that can help convert superoxide radicals to hydrogen peroxide.
  Peroxidase and catalase help break down hydrogen peroxide.
  Therefore, Superoxide dismutase is not the enzyme that releases reactive oxygen metabolites in lysosomes.
  The answer is NOT A, D or C.
Action: Answer("B")

  Balancing cusps are the ones that prevent lateral movements of the mandible.
  Supporting cusps and holding cusps are not commonly used dental terms.

  B: Fibroblasts

  Rests of Malassez are groups of epithelial cells that remain in the periodontal ligament after tooth development.

Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure used to access the root of a tooth.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the tooth roots have been exposed for 6 years.
  PDL (Periodontal Ligament) fibres attach the tooth to the surrounding bone.
  The cementum is the layer of hard tissue covering the root of the tooth.
  Dentin is the layer of tooth tissue beneath the enamel and cementum.
  Epithelium is a thin layer of tissue that covers body surfaces and lines internal organs.
  Co adaptation is the process by which two structures fit together perfectly.
  Based on this information, it is likely that the lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show PDL fibres attached to cementum, and not to dentin, since the root surface has been denuded for 6 years. Epithelium may be present adjacent to the previously denuded root surface, but it is not the most likely answer. Co adaptation to the remaining fibres is not likely to be seen since the roots have been denuded for 6 years.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:

  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure in which a flap of gum tissue is cut and moved to expose the underlying tooth root.
  Roots denuded for 6 years mean the roots have been exposed for a long time.
  PDL fibres (Periodontal Ligament fibers) attach the tooth to the bone.
  In normal conditions, PDL fibres attach the tooth to cementum which covers the tooth root.
  If the tooth root is denuded, the PDL fibres will attach to the exposed dentin.
  Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface is a sign of healing after the surgery.
  Co adaptation to the remaining fibers is a process of fibres adapting to the new position after surgery.
  Therefore, the answer is B: PDL fibres attached to dentin.

  A: VLDL
  B: LDL
  C: HDL
  D: Chylomicrons
Response 0:

  All of these are lipoproteins and transport lipids in the blood.
  Chylomicrons are the largest and least dense of all lipoproteins, while HDL is the smallest and most dense.
  VLDL and LDL are intermediate in size and density.
  Therefore, Chylomicrons have the least density among the given options.
Action: Answer("D")

  All of the given choices are lipoproteins.
  The density of lipoproteins is inversely proportional to the lipid content.

  Therefore, the answer is D: Chylomicrons.

  A: 0
  B: 3
  C: 5
  D: 8
Response 0:
Thought:
  The Bishop score is used to assess the readiness of the cervix for induction of labor.
  The score is based on the following factors:
    - Dilation of the cervix
    - Effacement of the cervix
    - Consistency of the cervix
    - Position of the cervix
    - Fetal station
  The possible score ranges from 0 to 13.
  In this case, the modified Bishop score can be calculated as follows:
    - Dilation: 1 cm (score of 0)
    - Effacement: 30% (score of 0)
    - Consistency: Soft (score of 1)
    - Position: Posterior (score of 0)
    - Fetal station: -1 (score of 2)
  Therefore, the modified Bishop score will be 3.

  The L:S ratio is the ratio of lecithin (a phospholipid found in pulmonary surfactant) to sphingomyelin (a phospholipid found in cell membranes).

Topic: Pathology
Question: Which of the following may be a feature of acromegaty?
Choices:
  A: Large tongue
  B: Micrognathia
  C: Hypoglycemia
  D: Crowded teeth
Response 0:
Thought:
  Acromegaly is a disorder caused by excessive production of growth hormone.
  The excess growth hormone stimulates the liver to produce insulin-like growth factor-1 (IGF-1) in excess, which causes excessive growth.
  The excess growth may result in enlarged organs, bones, cartilage, and soft tissues.
  A large tongue, crowded teeth, and an enlarged mandible are common features of acromegaly.
  Hypoglycemia is not a feature of acromegaly.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Acromegaly is a condition that results from excess growth hormone production from the anterior pituitary gland in adults.
  The condition leads to enlargement of the hands, feet, and face.
  Enlargement of the tongue is a common feature of acromegaly.
  Micrognathia is a condition where the lower jaw is undersized, which is not associated with acromegaly.
  Hypoglycemia is a condition where blood sugar levels are abnormally low, which is not associated with acromegaly.
  Crowded teeth is a condition where the teeth are too close together, which is not associated with acromegaly.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Large tongue.

Choices:
  A: Sensorimotor
  B: Pre-operational stage
  C: Concrete operations stage
  D: Formal operations stage

Question: What is the level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia?
Choices:
  A: 20 mg
  B: 200 mg
  C: 300 mg
  D: 3000 mg
Response 0:
Thought:
  Proteinuria is the presence of excess protein in the urine.
  Severe preeclampsia is a serious complication of pregnancy characterized by high blood pressure and damage to organs.
  Proteinuria is one of the diagnostic criteria for preeclampsia.
  According to the American College of Obstetricians and Gynecologists, a level of proteinuria of 300 mg in a 24-hour urine collection is diagnostic of severe preeclampsia.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 300 mg.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Preeclampsia is a pregnancy complication characterized by high blood pressure and damage to organs, usually kidneys.
  Proteinuria, or the presence of excess protein in the urine, is one of the diagnostic criteria for preeclampsia.
  Severe preeclampsia is a more severe form of preeclampsia that can lead to serious complications, including organ failure and death.
  The level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia is usually greater than 5 g in a 24-hour urine collection or 3+ on a urine dipstick.
  The given choices are in milligrams, so we need to convert the answer to grams.
  3000 mg is equal to 3 g, which is lower than the usual threshold for severe preeclampsia.
  Therefore, the answer is not D.
  20 mg is too low to diagnose severe preeclampsia.
  200 mg is also too low to diagnose severe preeclampsia.
  300 mg is still too low to diagnose severe preeclampsia.
  Therefore, none of the given choices are correct.

Question: Tourniquet test is used in daily follow-up of patients with:
Choices:
  A: Zika virus
  B: Dengue virus
  C: Chikungunya
  D: Swine flu
Response 0:
Thought:

  It is used to diagnose dengue fever.
  Zika virus, Chikungunya, and swine flu are not associated with the Tourniquet test.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Dengue virus.

Thought:
  Tourniquet test is a medical test used to check the capillary fragility in the patient's body.
  Capillary fragility is the ability of capillaries to resist pressure.
  Dengue virus is known to cause capillary fragility.
  Therefore, the tourniquet test is used in daily follow-up of patients with Dengue virus.
  The answer is B: Dengue virus.

  The test is done by inflating a blood pressure cuff on the upper arm to a point midway between the systolic and diastolic pressures for a few minutes.
  If more than 20 petechiae per square inch appear, the test is considered positive.
  Zika virus, swine flu, and chikungunya do not cause bleeding disorders.
  Dengue virus can cause bleeding disorders such as dengue hemorrhagic fever.
  Therefore, Tourniquet test is used in daily follow-up of patients with Dengue virus.

  Chondroblastoma is characterized by well-defined lytic lesion with calcification and is commonly seen in epiphysis of long bones.
  Osteoid osteoma is characterized by a small nidus and is commonly seen in the cortex of long bones.

Question: In lead poisoning, there is an inhibition of some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway. This is reflected by the accumulation of what substance in blood?
Choices:
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III
  B: Ferrochelatase
  C: Porphob I inogen
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid
Response 0:
Thought:
  The heme biosynthetic pathway is the process by which heme is produced in the body.
  In lead poisoning, some enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway are inhibited.
  The accumulation of what substance in blood reflects this inhibition?
  Uroporphyrinogen III and coproporphyrinogen III accumulate in congenital erythropoietic porphyria.
  Ferrochelatase is the final enzyme in the heme biosynthetic pathway and is inhibited in erythropoietic protoporphyria.
  Porphobinogen is synthesized from delta-aminolevulinic acid (ALA).
  The accumulation of ALA occurs in lead poisoning.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Delta amino levulinic acid.
Action: Answer("D")

  Delta amino levulinic acid (ALA) is the first intermediate in the heme biosynthetic pathway.

  Therefore, the answer is D: Delta amino levulinic acid.

Question: A 70 years old hypeensive patient with stage 5 chronic kidney disease was diagnosed recently with Type 2 diabetes mellitus. He doesn't want to take injectable insulin. Which of the following oral hypoglycemic agents will be preferred in this patient, which won't require any renal dose modification?
Choices:
  A: Linagliptin
  B: Repaglinide
  C: Vildagliptin
  D: Glimepiride
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient has stage 5 chronic kidney disease. This means the patient has an eGFR of less than 15 ml/min/1.73m2. 
  Metformin is contraindicated in patients with an eGFR less than 30 ml/min/1.73m2.
  Linagliptin and Vildagliptin are DPP4 inhibitors and have minimal renal excretion. Hence, they do not require dose modification in patients with renal impairment.
  Repaglinide is metabolized by the liver and is not affected by renal impairment.
  Glimepiride is metabolized in the liver and excreted in the urine. It should be avoided in patients with renal impairment.
  Therefore, the preferred oral hypoglycemic agent in this patient will be either A: Linagliptin or C: Vildagliptin.

  Glimepiride is metabolized in the liver and excreted in the bile, but it requires renal dose adjustments.
  Therefore, the preferred oral hypoglycemic agent for this patient would be either Linagliptin or Vildagliptin.

Question: Which of the following is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results?
Choices:
  A: Systematic random sampling
  B: Simple random sampling
  C: Stratified random sampling
  D: Cluster sampling
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Systematic random sampling is used when the population is too large.
  Simple random sampling is done by selecting individuals randomly from the population.
  Stratified random sampling is used to ensure that each subgroup of the population is represented in the sample.
  Cluster sampling is used when the population is divided into clusters.
  The question is asking about selecting patients based on potential factors that will affect the results, which means the sampling method should be tailored to these factors.
  The most appropriate sampling method is Stratified random sampling.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Systematic random sampling is used to select study participants in a systematic and predetermined order.
  Simple random sampling is used to select study participants randomly.
  Stratified random sampling is used to select study participants from different strata or subgroups based on specific criteria.
  Cluster sampling is used to select study participants in groups or clusters.
  The question is asking about selecting patients based on potential factors that will affect the results.
  Stratified random sampling is used to select study participants based on specific criteria.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.

- Stratified random sampling is when the population is divided into subgroups and individuals are randomly selected from each subgroup.
- Cluster sampling is when a population is divided into clusters and a certain number of clusters are randomly selected for the study.

Since the question is asking about selecting patients based on potential factors that will affect the results, the best sampling technique to use would be stratified random sampling because it allows for the selection of individuals from different subgroups. Therefore, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.

Question: A 10-year boy with dog bite unprovoked comes to you. Appropriate action is:
Choices:
  A: Give cell culture derived vaccine
  B: Withhold vaccine and observe dog for 10 days
  C: Kill dog and send brain for biopsy
  D: No fuher action is necessary
Response 0:
Thought:
  Dog bites can cause rabies.
  Rabies is a viral disease.
  The virus is transmitted through the saliva of infected animals.
  The incubation period of the disease is usually between 1 and 3 months.
  The disease is almost always fatal once symptoms appear.
  The best course of action is to take preventive measures.
  The appropriate action for an unprovoked dog bite is to give the cell culture-derived vaccine.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Give cell culture-derived vaccine.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:

  Rabies is a viral infection that can be fatal to humans.
  The risk of transmission depends on the type of exposure, the type of animal, and whether or not the animal is vaccinated.
  Unprovoked dog bites are considered a high risk for rabies transmission.
  The appropriate action would be to give post-exposure prophylaxis (PEP) to the boy.
  PEP includes both rabies immune globulin and rabies vaccine.
  The vaccine should be cell culture-derived, as it is more effective and safer than the older nerve tissue-derived vaccine.
  Observing the dog for 10 days is not appropriate in this case, as the risk of transmission is high and waiting could be deadly.
  Killing the dog and sending the brain for biopsy is not necessary in this case, as it may not be possible to determine if the dog was infected with rabies.
  No further action is not appropriate, as the boy needs PEP to prevent rabies.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Give cell culture derived vaccine.

Topic: Dental
Question: Which of the following has strong familial inheritance:
Choices:
  A: Functional class III
  B: Class I type I
  C: Class II div I
  D: Class II div II
Response 0:
Thought:
  Functional class III refers to a malocclusion where the lower jaw protrudes forward.
  Class I type I refers to a normal occlusion where the teeth are properly aligned.
  Class II div I and Class II div II both refer to malocclusions where the upper front teeth protrude forward.
  Familial inheritance means that a trait or characteristic is passed down from generation to generation within a family.
  Strong familial inheritance means that there is a high likelihood of a trait or characteristic being passed down within a family.
  Therefore, the answer is not A or B since they do not refer to malocclusions that have strong familial inheritance.
  Class II div I and Class II div II both have a strong familial inheritance.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Functional class III, Class I type I, Class II div I, and Class II div II are all types of malocclusion.
  Malocclusion is the misalignment or incorrect relation between the teeth of the two dental arches when they approach each other as the jaws close.
  Strong familial inheritance means that a trait or condition runs in the family.
  According to research, Class II div II has strong familial inheritance.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Class II div II.
Action: Answer("D")

Thought:
  Functional class III, class I type I, class II div I, and class II div II are types of malocclusion.

  Familial inheritance refers to the passing on of traits or characteristics from parents to their offspring.
  Therefore, I need to find which type of malocclusion is more likely to be inherited.
  According to studies, Class II malocclusion has strong familial inheritance.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 3:
Thought:
  Familial inheritance refers to the genetic tendency of certain dental issues to be passed down within families.
  Functional class III, class I type I, class II div I, and class II div II are all dental classifications that refer to the relationship between the upper and lower teeth and how they fit together.
